## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction. Classical kinetics relates dA/dt to powers of concentration A (rate laws), and explicit time dependence may arise from complex mechanisms, oscillating reactions, or externally driven conditions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (autocatalysis with finite resources)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., photolysis)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Consecutive reaction form: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate species in sequential reactions)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or heterogeneous kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence without explicit time → classical rate law dA/dt = k*A^n; check if time variable is irrelevant
- Negative dA_dt values (consumption) with magnitude proportional to A^n → nth-order decay kinetics
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches a nonzero value → reversible reaction with equilibrium concentration (dA/dt = k*(A - A_eq))
- Rate that increases then decreases with A → substrate inhibition or autocatalytic-then-limited mechanism, use rational functions like A/(1+A^2)
- Linear relationship between dA_dt and A → first-order kinetics; intercept indicates zero-order contribution or reverse reaction
- Rate proportional to A*(1-A/K) → logistic or autocatalytic kinetics with carrying capacity
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-elementary mechanism, catalyst deactivation, or externally varying conditions
- Square root or fractional power of A → chain reaction mechanisms or dissociative equilibrium steps
